JavaScript Math Object

=E2=9D=AE Previous Next =E2=9D=AF

The JavaScript Math object allows you to perform mathema= tical tasks on=20 numbers.

Example

Math.PI; =            // returns 3.141592653589793
Try it Yourself =C2=BB=

The Math Object

Unlike other objects, the Math object has no constructor.

The Math object is static.

All methods and properties can be used without creating a Math object fi= rst.

Math Properties (Constants)

The syntax for any Math property is : Math.<= i>property.

JavaScript provides 8 mathematical constants that can be accessed as Mat= h properties:

Example

Math.E &n= bsp;      // returns Euler's number
 Math.PI &= nbsp;     // returns PI
 Math.SQRT2&nbs= p;   // r= eturns the square root of 2
 Math.SQRT1_2&n= bsp; // returns the= square root of 1/2
 Math.LN2 =      // returns the natural logarithm of 2
 Math.LN10 = ;    // returns the natural logarithm of 10
 Math.LOG2E&nbs= p;   // r= eturns base 2 logarithm of E
 Math.LOG10E&nb= sp;  // return= s base 10 logarithm of E
Try it Yourself= =C2=BB

Math Methods

The syntax for Math any methods is : Math.method.(number)

Number to Integer

There are 4 common methods to round a number to an integer:

Math.round(x)Returns x rounded to its near= est integer
Math.ceil(x)Returns x rounded up to its nearest i= nteger
Math.floor(x)Returns x rounded down to its neares= t integer
Math.trunc(x)Returns the integer part of x (new in ES6)

Math.round()

Math.round(x) returns the nearest int= eger:

Example

Math.round(4.9);  &nbs= p; // returns 5
= Math.round(4.7);  &nbs= p; // returns 5
= Math.round(4.4);  &nbs= p; // returns 4
= Math.round(4.2);  &nbs= p; // returns 4
= Math.round(-4.2);  &nb= sp; // returns -4
Try it Yourself =C2= =BB

Math.ceil()

Math.ceil(x) returns the value of x r= ounded up to its nearest integer:

Example

Math.ceil(4.9);   = ;  // returns = 5
 Math.ceil(4.7);   = ;  // returns = 5
 Math.ceil(4.4);   = ;  // returns = 5
 Math.ceil(4.2);   = ;  // returns = 5
 Math.ceil(-4.2);  &nbs= p;  // returns= -4
Try it Yourself =C2= =BB

Math.floor()

Math.floor(x) returns the value of x = rounded down to its nearest integer:

Example

Math.floor(4.9);  &nbs= p; // returns 4
= Math.floor(4.7);  &nbs= p; // returns 4
= Math.floor(4.4);  &nbs= p; // returns 4
= Math.floor(4.2);  &nbs= p; // returns 4
= Math.floor(-4.2);  &nb= sp; // returns -5
Try it Yourself =C2= =BB

Math.trunc()

Math.trunc(x) returns the integer par= t of x:

Example

Math.trunc(4.9);  &nbs= p; // returns 4
= Math.trunc(4.7);  &nbs= p; // returns 4
= Math.trunc(4.4);  &nbs= p; // returns 4
= Math.trunc(4.2);  &nbs= p; // returns 4
= Math.trunc(-4.2);  &nb= sp; // returns -4
Try it Yourself =C2= =BB

Math.sign()

Math.sign(x) returns if x is negative= , null or positive:

Example

Math.sign(-4);   =  // returns -1
<= /span> Math.sign(0);   &= nbsp;// returns 0
Math.sign(4);   &= nbsp;// returns 1
Try it Yourself =C2= =BB

Math.trunc() and Math.sign() were added to JavaScript 2015 - ES6.

Math.pow()

Math.pow(x, y) returns the value of x= to the power of y:

Example

Math.pow(8, 2);      // returns 64
Try it Yourself =C2= =BB

Math.sqrt()

Math.sqrt(x) returns the square root = of x:

Example

Math.sqrt(64);   =    // returns = 8
Try it Yourself =C2= =BB

Math.abs()

Math.abs(x) returns the absolute (pos= itive) value of x:

Example

Math.abs(-4.7);   = ;  // returns = 4.7
Try it Yourself =C2= =BB

Math.sin()

Math.sin(x) returns the sine (a value= between -1 and 1) of the angle x (given in radians).

If you want to use degrees instead of radians, you have to convert degre= es to radians:

Angle in radians =3D Angle in degrees x PI / 180.

Example

Math.sin(90 * Math.PI / 180);     // returns 1 (the sine of 9= 0 degrees)
Try it Yourself =C2= =BB

Math.cos()

Math.cos(x) returns the cosine (a val= ue between -1 and 1) of the angle x (given in radians).

If you want to use degrees instead of radians, you have to convert degre= es to radians:

Angle in radians =3D Angle in degrees x PI / 180.

Example

Math.cos(0 * Math.PI / 180);     // returns 1 (the cos of 0 deg= rees)
Try it Yourself =C2= =BB

Math.min() and Math.max()

Math.min() and Math.max() can be used to find the lowest or highest value in = a list of arguments:

Example

Math.min(0, 150, 30, 20, -8, = -200);  = // returns -200
Try it Yourself =C2= =BB

Example

Math.max(0, 150, 30, 20, -8, = -200);  = // returns 150
Try it Yourself =C2= =BB

Math.random()

Math.random() returns a random number= between 0 (inclusive), and 1=20 (exclusive):

Example

Math.random();=      // returns a random number
Try it Yourself = =C2=BB

You will learn more about Math.random() in the next chapter of this tutorial.

The Math.log() Method

Math.log(x) returns the natural logar= ithm of x:

Example

Math.log(1);   &n= bsp;// returns 0
Try it Yourself =C2= =BB

The natural logarithm returns the time needed to reach a certain level o= f growth.

Math.E and Math.log() are twins.

How many times must we multiply Math.E to get 10?

Example

Math.log(10);   &= nbsp;// returns 2.302585= 092994046
Try it Your= self =C2=BB

The Math.log2() Method

Math.log2(x) returns the base 2 logar= ithm of x.

How many times must we multiply 2 to get 8?

Example

Math.log2(8);   &= nbsp;// returns 3
Try it Yourself =C2= =BB

The Math.log10() Method

Math.log10(x) returns the base 10 log= arithm of x.

How many times must we multiply 10 to get 1000?

Example

Math.log10(1000);  &nb= sp; // returns 3
Try it Yourself =C2= =BB

Math Object Methods

Method Description
abs(x) Returns the absolute value of x
acos(x)<= /a> Returns the arccosine of x, in radians
acosh(x= ) Returns the hyperbolic arccosine of x
asin(x)<= /a> Returns the arcsine of x, in radians
asinh(x= ) Returns the hyperbolic arcsine of x
atan(x)<= /a> Returns the arctangent of x as a numeric value between -PI/2 and PI= /2 radians
atan2(y= , x) Returns the arctangent of the quotient of its arguments
atanh(x= ) Returns the hyperbolic arctangent of x
cbrt(x)<= /a> Returns the cubic root of x
ceil(x)<= /a> Returns x, rounded upwards to the nearest integer
cos(x) Returns the cosine of x (x is in radians)
cosh(x)<= /a> Returns the hyperbolic cosine of x
exp(x) Returns the value of Ex
floor(x= ) Returns x, rounded downwards to the nearest integer
log(x) Returns the natural logarithm (base E) of x
max(x, y,= z, ..., n) Returns the number with the highest value
min(x, y,= z, ..., n) Returns the number with the lowest value
pow(x, y)= Returns the value of x to the power of y
random= () Returns a random number between 0 and 1
round(x= ) Rounds x to the nearest integer
sign(x)<= /a> Returns if x is negative, null or positive (-1, 0, 1)
sin(x) Returns the sine of x (x is in radians)
sinh(x)<= /a> Returns the hyperbolic sine of x
sqrt(x)<= /a> Returns the square root of x
tan(x) Returns the tangent of an angle
tanh(x)<= /a> Returns the hyperbolic tangent of a number
trunc(x= ) Returns the integer part of a number (x)
